text:
I don't give out 5 star ratings as often as I used to but we really enjoyed this salad and it is a definite keeper. I made a few small changes: chopped green leaf lettuce instead of romaine, roasted pecans instead of cashews, at least twice as much apple and pear and about 2 TBS less sugar. I wanted to have everything ready about an hour before it was time to toss everything together so I tossed the sliced apples and pears with some of the dressing. Besides staying nice and white they absorbed some of the wonderful dressing flavor. We enjoyed the Swiss cheese, but I want to try this with blue cheese next time. I think the sweetness of the dressing and the saltiness of the blue cheese would be perfect. 12/2004
Update 9/2007: I finally made this using blue cheese and I love it! My husband and I both liked it much better than the swiss cheese and this is the only way I will make it from now on.

Another tip: if you want to cut the apple and pear ahead of time, just toss it w/ a little of the dressing to prevent browning. Keep it in a separate container and add at the last minute.

text:
This was very popular at our family dinner. The combination was different and tasty, but next time I will cut down on the sugar for the dressing. It was a little too sweet.
*UPDATE* I have tried this recipe with swiss, cheddar, and parmesan...and I think it is best without any cheese at all. To save time, I will often use bottled lemon poppyseed dressing and prewashed organic greens. I also use what ever nuts I have on hand but I like slivered (not sliced) almonds the best. This salad is ALWAYS eaten all up at church potlucks.

text:
Made it for my office holiday party. It was a hit! Got lots of raves and a few people asked for the recipe. My modifications: (a) I doubled the recipe but instead of using 2 heads of romaine lettuce I used one head of romaine and 1 bag of spinach. (b)Omitted the Swiss cheese. (c) Instead of cashews I added toasted pecans (toasted myself). Nuts such as pecans and walnuts seem to match the fruit and season better. (d) I added some dried cherries along with the dried cranberries. (d)Despite having doubled the salad I only needed half as much dressing because the dressing was on the side.

Having the dressing on the side worked great. I used less, the salad didn't get soggy and the leftovers kept better. The leftovers were actually minimal. I made a huge bowl. Since the original recipes makes 12 - 1 cup servings, I made roughly 24 cups. At the end of the evening the rest fit tightly in a 3-cup Ziplock plastic storage container.

text:
FANTASTIC!  The lemon poppyseed dressing is absolutely delicious.  Be sure to use freshly squeezed lemons and not the stuff out of the yellow plastic containers - - it does make a difference. I used butter lettuce instead of romaine, but otherwise I followed the recipe exactly.  The pears, apples, cheese, and cashews combined perfectly with the lemon dressing.  One word of caution - - this fed three hungry adults (two helpings for the men).  So don't be fooled by the "serves 12".  Your family and guests will go back for seconds, trust me!

text:
This recipe is very yummy! 
I gave this a three star rating because I changed it a bit as follows:

1/4 cup sugar
1 tablespoon dijon
1/3 cup veg. oil

Everything else I kept the same. I felt that there was way to much sugar, and oil. With fiddling with the amounts I found it can increase the actual taste over sweetness. 
Increasing the Dijon mustard, and decreasing the sugar brings out the lemon, and Dijon tangy-ness that creates a more subtle taste.

As others have said there is way too much dressing for one salad but I always manage to use up the leftovers.

If I use a standard bag of pre cut/washed romaine lettuce then I halve the dressing recipe.  I often use 2 pears instead of the 1 apple, 1 pear. text:
Wow - what a fabulous, yet elegant salad to serve at a holiday get togther or anytime for that matter! It's got a wonderful combination of flavors, colors and textures. The dressing is absolutely delicious and the proportions are spot-on, if I had to change anything I would use just a little less sugar. But other than that is was perfect. I just threw everything into a mini-food processor and gave it a whirl then poured it into a container and added the poppy seeds last and just shook it up. I used butter lettuce vs. romaine and toasted walnuts vs. cashews. I soaked my apples and pears in lemon water so they wouldn't brown. The Swiss cheese was very good and next time I might try a blue cheese or even a feta. Great recipe that's very easy and something you'll want to make again!

text:
Easily one of my favorite salads. My modifications: 1) I minced the onion very fine since I don't have a food processor. 2) I also used walnuts instead of cashews and it goes so well with cranberries. 3) I cube the apples in advance and dump them into a container with the dressing, This way when I'm preparing lunch for work in the morning I just scoop out the apples onto a bed of lettuce, toss in some nuts and berries, and I have a fantastic salad!

Wow - what a fabulous, yet elegant salad to serve at a holiday get togther or anytime for that matter! It's got a wonderful combination of flavors, colors and textures. The dressing is absolutely delicious and the proportions are spot-on, if I had to change anything I would use just a little less sugar.  But other than that is was perfect. I made this at the last moment with ingredients I had on hand, but it was awesome! The lemon dressing I had made the night before was awful and I had company coming so I had to improvise. I found this recipe and made a few changes. I didn't have an onion but the dressing needed something so I substitued minced ginger-wow! This was amazing! I also kept my greens, crunchies, fruit and dressing separate so my guests could add what they wanted. Six people finished the whole salad.  I used 1/3 cup walnuts, 1/3 cup almonds and 2 T flax seed-toasted-for my crunchies. The fruit I had on hand was 2 clementines, 2 granny smiths and 1/4 cup dried cranberries. My salad greens included 5 oz. of baby lettuces and half a package of spinach. Can't wait to make this again-thanks!

text:
I made this for my family and everyone raved about how good it was.  While the quality of your ingredients are always important, I believe it is fundamental to this recipe.  I used Gala apple, and red pear.  The pear was so sweet.  I took 6 slices of deli cheese and cut them into matchsticks rather than grated.  Other than that, I followed the recipe exactly.  I did not dress the salad, but kept the dressing in a container.  Refrigerating the leftover dressing is a BONUS that you can use on other salads.  THIS recipe is going to make its way to some of my holiday menus.  ABSOLUTELY wonderful, easy, & sure to be in my regular rotation. Thanks for a great dish!

text:
I served this salad with our uncle's 96th birthday dinner, and everyone loved it!  It reminded me more of spring than of winter--the fresh tart/sweet flavors of the lemon juice/sugar mixture on the crisp greens woke my taste buds up and put them in a happy mood for the rest of the dinner! If you don't have a pear, just put in extra apple; and instead of just the dried cranberries, I used a dried berry mix consisting of cranberries, cherries and blueberries, which were great. I will definitely be using this as one of my main salad recipes, and I would imagine this will taste awesome on a hot summer day on our screened porch in August.

text:
Made this last night for a holiday dinner party, and it was excellent! I doubled the recipe for a party of 8, and we had about two cups leftover. Our guests unanimously raved about this, and all wanted the recipe. I used Honey Crisp apples and Bosc pears. Subbed walnut pieces for the cashews and used about half of the listed amount of shredded Swiss. Also, per the suggestion of another reviewer, I used red onion to give the dressing a little pink color. I cut up the pears and apples in advance and tossed them in a several TBS of dressing, and I later tossed this with the rest of the ingredients with one more TBS of dressing, and that was more than enough. I had tons of dressing leftover, as many other people have noted, so unless you like having it leftover, you can cut those amounts in half and still have plenty. Great recipe - this salad will be made very regularly. Thanks!

Made this salad for Thanksgiving and it got raves from everyone that tried it. The dressing definitely makes the salad special. I did make a few changes to what I put in the salad - used feta instead of swiss and toasted slivered almonds (was all I had), but other than that I followed the recipe. I recommend the feta with this salad combination. It worked very well. I made the dressing per the recipe except I didn't have dijon mustard so use regular yellow mustard. The dressing makes ALOT. My advice - put the dressing on the side and let your family/guests put it on themselves. Not eveyone ate the salad and what was left over had to be thrown away because I had put the dressing on the salad prior to serving and it wilted. Excellent recipe though. If you are a salad lover, I definitely recommend it.

We love this salad!  The tip to chop the fruits in advance and put them in a bit of the dressing to keep from browning really works! I had put aside a bit of the fruit (ok, I HID it so I could have a salad later!) - and just mixed it in with some lefover turkey, celery, onion, mixed a little of the poppyseed dressing w/mayo - and just ate the best turkey salad sandwich ever!  Dressing is deeeelicious!

text:
This is an amazing salad!!! I've made it many times for Sunday and holiday dinners. The only change I made was to cut down on the sugar just a bit, but it was still fantastic!  Before adding the poppy seeds to the dressing, I reserve a little of it and add it to the cut-up bits of apple and pear - this keeps them from turning brown. The other thing I love about this salad is that all the add-ons,i.e., cheese, cashews, etc. can be prepared ahead of time.  And all you have to do is to toss it altogether right before serving!

Glad I read the other reviews first. I doubled the dressing recipe, using only 1/2 cup of sugar and it was perfect. Vegetable oil is not something I use, so I substituted 1/3 cup olive oil and 1/3 cup canola oil. I used the leftover dressing on plain spinach and lettuce the next day and it was great. The cheese and nuts are nice in a salad but I do not like swiss or cashews. I used sliced almonds and blue cheese. The cranberries and fruit were nice. This recipe will be added to my favorites.

text:
I've made this recipe several times, making alterations after the 1st time. The dressing is perfect as is (make sure to use fresh lemon juice). However we have found that blue cheese and walnuts taste better to us. I give the walnuts a quick "roast" in the microwave (2 minutes)for the best flavor.    I make the dressing several hours in advance and coat the fruit with some of it to also set during that time.    We like a spring mix instead of romaine, but if that is all I have I've found it works better if you chop it rather finely instead of using Caesar salad sized pieces.

As written, I give 3 stars. It's too sweet for my taste. If interested, I made a couple changes on the 2nd go with this recipe. I omitted the sugar completely, and used the juice from the can of mandarin oranges.I also used the oranges. They are VERY tasty in salads with the sweet /savory appeal. Overall, a nice base recipe. Even better with minor tweaking.

I gave it 5/5 stars because it just a great salad as it or with some tweaks.  I did forget to put the mustard in this time, and I used walnuts only because thats what I had on hand.  I cut the sugar in half, and didn't add cheese. I also added about 2 Tbsp of red wine vinegar.  Turned out great friends and family loved it.  A few wanted the recipe so I sent a link to them from here.  Next time I think I'll add seedless grapes, kiwi, and/or other fruit with an assortment of nuts. text:
Great!  I've hade a lemon poppyseed dressing that was creamy so I was happy to see that although sweet, it is not creamy (i.e. less fattening!).  I don't have a food processor, so I just mixed quickly.  Don't know if having a foor processor would alleviate problem with separation, if only a bit, but still good.  The dressing is too much for the amount of lettuce I have.  I don't think you'll need that much unless you want it smothered.  Didn't add the onion, used dried cherries rather than dried cranberries, blue cheese rather than Swiss (although as another reviewer suggested, may not include cheese at all next time), used olice oil used slivered almonds rather than cashews.

text:
I made this for Thanksgiving and it was a huge success.  There were a few who did not try it initially, but quickly helped themselves after they heard all the raves from those who did try it.  The dressing is so light and goes perfectly with the ingredients in the salad ... although you don't need to double the dressing because there's more than enough even when you double the salad ingredients.  I went with 2 bags of Romaine and doubled everything else to comfortably feed 14 people.  After cutting the fruit, I tossed it into a little bit of the dressing to keep the fruit from turning brown.  Not until I was ready to serve the salad did I toss a little more dressing into the salad.  Again, I had lots of dressing left over.  The swiss cheese and cashews may sound strange, but they are absolutely delicious in the salad.  This salad perfectly complements a heavy Thanksgiving/Christmas meal.

text:
Somehow Swiss cheese in such a salad skipped my imagination. Thanks for the great idea! ****QUICK TIP*****: if you have a hand blender (stick version), place all dressing ingredients in a jar and blend it in that. Slowly lift the blender wand up towards the mouth of the jar. With this method, the oil does not have to be drizzled in that way (same with mayo). Have a tall cup with sudsy water (or maybe another jar). The blender wand cleans up in no time at all. Simple. Less clean up.  Store leftover dressing right in the jar you mixed it in!  Have another salad with greens, fruit, nuts, and possibly cheese of choice later in the week.... and the dressing will be all ready!

text:
I have an almost identical recipe from another site & have been making this salad for many years.  It is outstanding and always gets many recipe requests.  I prefer to leave the skins on the fruit & always use Honeycrisp apples and red pears. I also think that using finely grated swiss cheese is really important as it is a strong tasting cheese & when shredded finely, balances nicely with the lemony dressing and fruits.  Be sure to give this one a try!

text:
I've made this several times.  I used to save it for large gatherings, but I decided that's just silly.  I make the dressing, and put it in a container to use as needed.  When out of Dijon mustard I've used grainy (German-style) mustard.  I had to taste and play with the amount, but it still turned out fine.  I prefer toasted sliced almonds or sunflower seeds to cashews.  And we like a strong tasting cheese, like Gorgonzola.  You can play with the fruits, too.  

Thanks for this recipe, Nora LaCroix.  It's a keeper!

text:
I made this salad exactly as given and it was great! (I think it is more interesting if used with a lettuce blend.) Also, if you want to make the salad a couple hours ahead of time, put the diced fruit on the bottom of the bowl, drizzle a little of the dressing on the fruit, stir,(so the fruit doesn't turn brown) and then put the lettuce, then everything else on top.  Pour the dressing on and toss when ready to serve.

text:
Pretty good.... While not one of the best salads I've ever had, this was quite yummy nonetheless. Having said this, I am not a huge fan of pears OR cashews but I enjoyed the combination of both in this! It's the gritty texture of pears that I don't particularly care for, but I found that Comice pears are just what I like - extra sweet with a soft / silky flesh and creamy bite (perfect!). I LOVED this variety of pear in this salad and found that it perfectly complemented the crisp, sweet-tart Honeycrisp apple I paired it with! Although I probably won't serve this salad often (again, this was good but not WOW good...), I will almost definitely add the dressing recipe to my "keeper" file. It was absolutely delicious, can be used on a variety of items (I'm trying coleslaw next!) and it kept my fruit fresh and bright until I was ready to toss it with everything else (as LINDABTX did, I also added a bit of dressing to my pre-cut fruit beforehand). For these reasons alone, I'm glad I stumbled upon your recipe! Thanks for sharing, Nora! :-)

I made this salad twice over the holidays.  The first time I made it I used two heads of romaine lettuce and made the dressing as directed.  The salad was swimming in the dressing!  The second time I also used two heads of romaine and cut the dressing in half and it was perfect.  I also decided to use craisins instead of regular dried cranberries and liked it very well.  A great tip I read from another reviewer was to store the chopped apple and pear in the dressing when transporting the salad so they don't turn brown - great idea!

text:
The dressing was fabulous - the actual salad was just OK. I made 1/2 the amount of the dressing (and used about only half of that). I also only added aout 3 tbsp. of olive oil instead of what was called for. I added some fresh minced garlic and 2 tsp. finely chopped basil to the dressing. i refrigerated that for a couple of hours to all for the flavors to blend. I love the sweet and tangy taste of the dressing and prefer lemon juice to vinegar in dressings. As for the salad itself - I did not peel the fruit - as I wanted the peel to add color to the salad. I thinly sliced the fruit and let them sit in 2 tsp. lemon juice to make sure it would not brown/oxidize until I was ready to put the salad together. I left out the swiss cheese, but added a sliced red onion. I guess I did not like the pears and apples in my salad - I prefer vegetables in my salad. if I make it again - I will substitute red, and yellow peppers for the pears and apples. I would keep the craisins and toss in a can of drained manderine oranges - as I do not mind those in salads.

text:
This was so easy and yummy.  I prepped  a baggie of the cranberries and nuts. I subbed pecan pieces since I had them on hand.  Then, the next morning, I made the dressing and kept in a shaker.  A few hours before eating, I peeled and cored the apples (used two, since pears were not ripe enough) and dressed the salad. The apples really help up under the lemony dressing.  I also omitted the cheese to keep this lighter. I also required more than one head of romaine for the amount of dressing.I would make all types of versions of this salad again. It was a hit. Was even able to use leftover apple/nut/berry dressing parts with fresh romaine for lunches the next day.

text:
A simple, elegant salad that make a perfect complement to a range of both traditional and non-traditional holiday dinners.  The flavors of these seasonal fruits -- pears, apples, cranberries and citrus  --  with poppy seeds and lettuce not only play beautifully together, but make a festive presentation at Christmastime. I also like the idea of having the fruit and greens in together in one dish, making this salad equally useful as a companion side and a stand-alone side (to go with, say, lasagna or some other one-dish entree).  I have made this several times and will be making it again this year. I make the recipe as-is, usually minus the cheese, although it is excellent with Gorgonzola, which I think is an improvement over Swiss.

I have had a recipe similar to this for years.  When I bring it to a party or make it for company, people always rave about it and ask for the recipe.  The only difference is in the dressing.  It has less lemon juice and uses red wine vinegar: 
 c sugar
1/3c red wine vinegar
2 T lemon juice
2 T finely chopped onion
 t salt
2/3 c vegetable oil
2-3 t poppy seed

I needed to make the salad for my culinary class and this recipe was perfect for the job; we were doing a mystery ingredients thing like on chopped or master chief. I didn't have all the ingredients so I had to substitute some things but in the in it came out great. 1) instead of poppy seeds I use roasted sunflower seeds, cashews into cornflakes(one of the mystery items we has to use), the berries into blackberries(same as the cornflakes), I needed to make the salad for my culinary class and this recipe was perfect for the job; we were doing a mystery ingredients thing like on chopped or master chief. I didn't have all the ingredients so I had to substitute some things but in the in it came out great. 1) instead of poppy seeds I use roasted sunflower seeds, cashews into cornflakes(one of the mystery items we has to use), the bried berries into raisins, all American cheese shredded, and that about it but I soaked the apples and pears in lemon juice to keep it from browning. I added blackberries as a topping. It came out looking delicious, too bad I forgot to take a pic. 

I would definitely make this again, in fact I am, I'm making at home this weekend this time cause my mom wanted to try it.

text:
1/2 cup of sugar is WAY too much- almost sickeningly sweet.  I remade the dressing with only 1 tablespoon of sugar, and thought it was much better!
I also use candied pecans instead of cashews, spring mix instead of romaine, and I leave the peel on the apple and pear.  It's delicious with or without cheese.
With those adjustments it is one of my family's favorite salads!  We make it every Christmas.
Next time I am going to try olive oil instead of vegetable oil.

text:
I made this salad with three changes.  First, I substituted carmalized pecans, coarsest chopped, for the cashews,  Second,  my apple of choice was Honey Crisp, unpeeled and  the pear variety was Bosc, unpeeled.  By leaving the skins on,the salad appeared more vibrant and hence more pleasing to the eye,  Third, in addition to the Romaine, I added green leaf lettuce because I wanted more variety to the lettuce base. Red leaf lettuce would have added more color, but lacks the crispy texture of the leafy green lettuce.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I've been making this recipe for years perfect for Thanksgiving because dressing and fruit can be prepared early in morning and doesn't take frig space; only difference in my recipe and this one I use two pears and two granny smith apples with skin on. Make dressing first. Then cut fruit and place in large salad bowl. I just pour all the dressing over fruit in morning and place Press & Seal over fruit to stop it from browning. Wash & Dry Romaine crisp in Frig. Measure out 1/2 cup whole cashews and 1/2 cup cranraisins seal in baggies. When ready to serve. I tear up lettuce into bite sized pieces toss with fruit/dressing mixture. Sprinkle cashews & cranraisins toss. Then top with finely shredded swiss cheese (much like Parmesan a Caesar Salad)

I did enjoy this recipe but I did make a few changes such as I used strawberries and mandarin oranges although I think you can just use whatever fruit is in season and it would be great!  I also used feta cheese shredded as I could not find swiss shredded but next time I may try swiss.  I also used mixed baby greens and the mistake I made was mixing up the salad minus the dressing and drove it to a BBQ about 1/2 hr away and then it sat for another 1/2 hr before we ate and it had wilted a lot.  I did dress it then but only half of the dressing as it makes sooo much!  I am not sure if I like the lemony flavour or not I used bottled lemon juice so I may cut back next time.  I also may use romaine next time as well but Caesar salad was also being served so I wanted to be different.  Overall the mixture of flavours and textures was very yummy therefor 4 1/2 stars!

The use of lemon (overall alkalizing)rather than vinegar is a nice change with the same results, balancing the acid of the sugar just so. We like it enough that I have a carafe of dressing on hand, a bowl of chopped fruits tossed with a bit of dressing to prevent oxidation, and greens with other ingredients in separate bowl. It can last up to 2 days without noticeable deterioration. Thank you for sharing.
